# Status

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (File Quit app exit): the File menu now exposes `Quit` after Close. `default_editor_menu` registers `Command::Quit` with executable `Ctrl+Q`; unlike document-mutating File commands, Quit remains enabled while PIE is active. `EditorShell::route_menu_command` routes Quit to `handle_quit_request()`, which records a one-shot app-exit request consumed at the next winit event boundary through the existing `ActiveEventLoop::exit()` path used by `CloseRequested`. Quit does not close/reset the current document and does not clear the adopted save source. Tests cover registry resolution, host projection/FIFO/enablement, keyboard Ctrl+Q parity, shell routing, and stale unrouted-command coverage. `plans/BASELINE.md` narrows the File/menu execution surface accordingly. **Not changed:** no unsaved-changes prompt/confirmation, no graceful shutdown save flow, no disk/project/template creation, no File Close reset semantics, no OS/system clipboard integration, no authoritative CAD graph/projection/render content mutation, no undo/redo or dirty-state integration, no plugin runtime/action execution, no command palette, no host->shell FIFO replacement, no conflict resolution/keybinding editor/fatal gating, no Cargo, scheduler, dispatch automation, or task arming. **Verification:** `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; `git diff --check` clean. `cargo check -p rge-editor-ui -p rge-editor-egui-host -p rge-editor-shell --lib` remains locally blocked before crate type-checking by this machine's missing MSVC `link.exe` while compiling proc-macro crates.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (File Close current document): the File menu now exposes `Close` after Save As New Project. `default_editor_menu` registers `Command::Close` with executable `Ctrl+W`, enabled only while Editing alongside New/Open/Save/Save-As. `EditorShell::route_menu_command` routes Close to `handle_close_file_request()`, which reuses `replace_world(KernelWorld::new())` to close the current document into a fresh unsourced empty world without exiting the application. The reset clears the adopted save source, entity selection, shell-local clipboard, render content, PIE snapshot, and command bus; the fresh world gets default `TimeScale`. Tests cover registry resolution, disabled accelerator behavior, host projection/FIFO/enablement, keyboard Ctrl+W parity, and shell routing. `plans/BASELINE.md` narrows the File/menu execution surface accordingly. **Not changed:** no app quit/exit behavior, unsaved-changes prompt, disk/project/template creation, Save-As-new-project completion, OS/system clipboard integration, authoritative CAD graph/projection/render deletion or duplication, undo/redo or dirty-state integration for File Close, plugin runtime/action execution, command palette, host->shell FIFO replacement, conflict resolution/keybinding editor/fatal gating, Cargo, scheduler, dispatch automation, or task arming. **Verification:** `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; `git diff --check` clean. `cargo check -p rge-editor-ui -p rge-editor-egui-host -p rge-editor-shell --lib` remains locally blocked before crate type-checking by this machine's missing MSVC `link.exe` while compiling proc-macro crates.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (Edit Cut selected entities): the Edit menu now exposes `Cut` between Select All and Copy. `default_editor_menu` registers `Command::Cut` with executable `Ctrl+X`, enabled only while Editing with a non-empty entity selection. `EditorShell::route_menu_command` routes Cut to `cut_selected_entities()`, which copies selected legacy component blobs into the shell-local entity clipboard and then delegates deletion to the existing bounded wrapper-world `delete_selected_entities()` path. The source entities are despawned from the wrapper world, entity selection is cleared, face selections for deleted entities are pruned, and Paste can recreate fresh wrapper-world entities from the copied blobs. Tests cover registry resolution, disabled accelerator behavior, host projection/FIFO/enablement, keyboard Ctrl+X parity, and shell routing including Paste-after-Cut. `plans/BASELINE.md` narrows the generalized Edit menu and clipboard surface accordingly. **Not changed:** no OS/system clipboard integration, typed kernel component cloning, authoritative CAD graph/projection/render cut/paste, undo/redo or dirty-state integration for Cut, plugin runtime/action execution, command palette, host->shell FIFO replacement, conflict resolution/keybinding editor/fatal gating, Cargo, scheduler, dispatch automation, or task arming. **Verification:** `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; `git diff --check` clean. `cargo check -p rge-editor-ui -p rge-editor-egui-host -p rge-editor-shell --lib` remains locally blocked before crate type-checking by this machine's missing MSVC `link.exe` while compiling proc-macro crates.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (Edit Copy/Paste selected entities): the Edit menu now exposes `Copy` and `Paste` after Select All. `default_editor_menu` registers `Command::Copy` with executable `Ctrl+C`, enabled only while Editing with a non-empty entity selection, and `Command::Paste` with executable `Ctrl+V`, enabled only while Editing with a non-empty shell clipboard. `PredicateContext` now carries `has_clipboard_entities`, filled by `EditorShell::predicate_context()`. `World::clone_entity_blobs` / `spawn_with_component_blobs` provide the shared legacy-blob clone substrate, and `duplicate_entity_blobs` now reuses it. `EditorShell::route_menu_command` routes Copy to `copy_selected_entities()` and Paste to `paste_copied_entities()`: Copy stores cloned legacy component blobs in a shell-local clipboard; Paste spawns fresh wrapper-world entities, selects the pasted entities, and clears face selection because no authoritative face-ID remapping exists. The clipboard is cleared by `replace_world`, including File New and scene Open. Tests cover registry resolution, disabled accelerator behavior, host projection/FIFO/enablement, keyboard Ctrl+C/Ctrl+V parity, world clone/spawn helpers, shell routing, and File New clipboard clearing. `plans/BASELINE.md` narrows the generalized Edit menu and clipboard surface accordingly. **Not changed:** no Cut semantics, OS/system clipboard integration, typed kernel component cloning, authoritative CAD graph/projection/render copy/paste, undo/redo or dirty-state integration for Copy/Paste, plugin runtime/action execution, command palette, host->shell FIFO replacement, conflict resolution/keybinding editor/fatal gating, Cargo, scheduler, dispatch automation, or task arming. **Verification:** `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; `git diff --check` clean. `cargo check -p rge-editor-ui -p rge-editor-egui-host -p rge-editor-shell --lib` remains locally blocked before crate type-checking by this machine's missing MSVC `link.exe` while compiling proc-macro crates.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (File New empty scene command): the File menu now exposes `New` before Open. `default_editor_menu` registers `Command::NewFile` with executable `Ctrl+N`, enabled only while Editing. `EditorShell::route_menu_command` routes New to `handle_new_file_request()`, which reuses `replace_world(KernelWorld::new())` to reset to a fresh unsourced empty world. The reset clears the adopted save source, entity selection, render content, PIE snapshot, and command bus, and the fresh world gets default `TimeScale`. Tests cover registry resolution, disabled accelerator behavior, host projection/FIFO/enablement, keyboard Ctrl+N parity, and shell routing. `plans/BASELINE.md` narrows the File/menu execution surface accordingly. **Not changed:** no unsaved-changes prompt, disk/project/template creation, Save-As-new-project completion, Cut/Copy/Paste semantics, clipboard, authoritative CAD graph/projection/render deletion or duplication, undo/redo or dirty-state integration for Edit content mutations, plugin runtime/action execution, command palette, host->shell FIFO replacement, conflict resolution/keybinding editor/fatal gating, Cargo, scheduler, dispatch automation, or task arming. **Verification:** `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; `git diff --check` clean. `cargo check -p rge-editor-ui -p rge-editor-egui-host -p rge-editor-shell --lib` remains locally blocked before crate type-checking by this machine's missing MSVC `link.exe` while compiling proc-macro crates.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (Edit Duplicate selected entities): the Edit menu now exposes `Duplicate` after Delete. `default_editor_menu` registers `Command::Duplicate` with executable `Ctrl+D`, enabled only while Editing with a non-empty entity selection. `World::duplicate_entity_blobs` spawns a fresh entity and clones legacy component blobs from the selected source entity; typed kernel components are intentionally not cloned because there is no safe generic clone path. `EditorShell::route_menu_command` routes Duplicate to `duplicate_selected_entities()`, which duplicates selected wrapper-world entities, selects the new duplicates, and clears face selection because no authoritative face-ID remapping exists. Tests cover registry resolution, disabled accelerator behavior, host projection/FIFO/enablement, keyboard Ctrl+D parity, world duplicate, and shell routing. `plans/BASELINE.md` narrows the generalized menu-command execution item accordingly. **Not changed:** no Cut/Copy/Paste semantics, clipboard, authoritative CAD graph/projection/render duplication, undo/redo or dirty-state integration for duplication, plugin runtime/action execution, command palette, host->shell FIFO replacement, conflict resolution/keybinding editor/fatal gating, Cargo, scheduler, dispatch automation, or task arming. **Verification:** `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; `git diff --check` clean. `cargo check -p rge-editor-ui -p rge-editor-egui-host -p rge-editor-shell --lib` remains locally blocked before crate type-checking by this machine's missing MSVC `link.exe` while compiling proc-macro crates.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (Edit Delete selected entities): the Edit menu now exposes `Delete` after Select All. `default_editor_menu` registers `Command::Delete` with executable plain `Delete`, enabled only while Editing with a non-empty entity selection. `World::despawn` removes an entity from both the kernel world and the legacy blob view, including legacy component blobs; `EditorShell::route_menu_command` routes Delete to `delete_selected_entities()`, which deletes selected wrapper-world entities, clears entity selection, and prunes face selections for deleted entities. Tests cover registry resolution, disabled accelerator behavior, host projection/FIFO/enablement, keyboard Delete parity, world despawn, and shell routing. `plans/BASELINE.md` narrows the generalized menu-command execution item accordingly. **Not changed:** no Cut/Copy/Paste/Duplicate semantics, clipboard, authoritative CAD graph/projection/render deletion, undo/redo or dirty-state integration for deletion, plugin runtime/action execution, command palette, host->shell FIFO replacement, conflict resolution/keybinding editor/fatal gating, Cargo, scheduler, dispatch automation, or task arming. **Verification:** `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; `git diff --check` clean. `cargo check -p rge-editor-ui -p rge-editor-egui-host -p rge-editor-shell --lib` remains locally blocked before crate type-checking by this machine's missing MSVC `link.exe` while compiling proc-macro crates.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (Edit Select All menu command): the Edit menu now exposes `Select All` after Undo / Redo. `default_editor_menu` registers `Command::SelectAll` with executable `Ctrl+A`, guarded by a new `PredicateContext::has_selectable_entities` bit plus `is_editing` so the binding displays but only fires for a non-empty world in Editing. `EditorShell::predicate_context()` fills that bit from `world.entity_count()`, and `EditorShell::route_menu_command` routes Select All to `select_all_entities()`, replacing entity selection with the deterministic live `World::entities()` set without mutating world contents, CAD geometry, face selection, or the undo stack. Tests cover registry resolution, disabled accelerator behavior, host projection/FIFO/enablement, keyboard Ctrl+A parity, shell context publication, and shell routing. `plans/BASELINE.md` narrows the generalized menu-command execution item accordingly. **Not changed:** no Cut/Copy/Paste/Delete/Duplicate semantics, clipboard, plugin runtime/action execution, command palette, host->shell FIFO replacement, conflict resolution/keybinding editor/fatal gating, Cargo, scheduler, dispatch automation, or task arming. **Verification:** `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; `git diff --check` clean. `cargo check -p rge-editor-ui -p rge-editor-egui-host -p rge-editor-shell --lib` remains locally blocked before crate type-checking by this machine's missing MSVC `link.exe`.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (View camera zoom commands): the View menu now exposes `Zoom In` and `Zoom Out` beside Reset Camera / Frame Scene. `default_editor_menu` registers `Command::ZoomIn` and `Command::ZoomOut` with plain `PageUp` / `PageDown` executable accelerators, raising the canonical executable menu accelerator count from six to eight. `EditorShell::route_menu_command` routes those commands to new infallible camera helpers that preserve target, view direction, up vector, FOV, and clip planes while scaling eye-target distance by inverse factors (`0.8` / `1.25`), with a finite fallback for degenerate eye-target vectors. Tests cover registry resolution, host projection/FIFO, keyboard PageUp/PageDown parity, direct camera math, and shell menu routing. `plans/BASELINE.md` narrows the broader camera-state UI item accordingly. **Not changed:** no command palette, plugin runtime/action execution, host->shell FIFO replacement, conflict resolution/keybinding editor/fatal gating, Cargo, scheduler, dispatch automation, or task arming. **Verification:** `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; `git diff --check` clean. `cargo check -p rge-editor-shell --lib` remains locally blocked before crate type-checking by this machine's missing MSVC `link.exe`.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (PowerShell CI handoff-test hardening): the `powershell` workflow failure on `3fc8b0c` is fixed. `.github/workflows/powershell.yml` now checks out full history (`fetch-depth: 0`) because `HandoffScopeHistoricalSmoke.Tests.ps1` intentionally reads older commits with `git diff-tree`; the prior depth-1 checkout made those commits ambiguous in CI. `Test-HandoffPacket.ps1` now trims header/list field values and accepts CRLF on `INCIDENTAL_OK: true`, so CRLF-authored packets validate the same as LF-authored packets. `HandoffPacketValidator.Tests.ps1` writes each synthetic packet into a fresh per-test OS temp directory, outside Pester's shared `TestDrive`, so `.meta.json` sidecars and fixed packet filenames cannot leak across tests/runs. **Not changed:** no queue/guard/auto behavior, Rust source, Cargo, menu behavior, scheduler, or task arming. **Verification:** focused Pester (`HandoffPacketValidator`, `HandoffScopeHistoricalSmoke`) 15/15; full `tools/dispatch-tests` Pester 392/392; touched-file PSScriptAnalyzer 0 findings; `git diff --check` clean. Focused tests now pin both sides: the Play menu shows Space/Escape hints, while Play/View entries still carry no executable accelerator and the global accelerator table remains exactly the five File/Edit bindings. **Not changed:** no playback key routing, no View Reset Camera binding, no dynamic labels, no menu-click FIFO replacement, no plugin-menu behavior, no scheduler/dispatch automation/Rust workspace architecture. **Verification:** `cargo test -p rge-editor-ui --lib` 100/100; `cargo test -p rge-editor-egui-host --lib` 24/24; `cargo +nightly fmt --all -- --check` clean; architecture lints PASS; `git diff --check` clean; `.ai/dispatch.verify.ps1` exit 0.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (ADR-121 queue claim TTL guard): the queue claim TTL is now explicit and configurable as `Invoke-AiDispatchQueue.ps1 -HandoffClaimTtlSeconds`, defaulting to 43200 seconds (12 hours). The queue threads that value through both claim acquisition/reclaim and release helper invocations, so a normal long orchestrator run should not outlive its ADR-121 live claim before release. `AI_DISPATCH_AUTOMATION.md` and ADR-121 document the tradeoff: this is not a background renewal loop; a crashed queue leaves the claim stale only after the configured TTL. `tools/dispatch-tests/AutonomousCodexExecutorDryRun.Tests.ps1` pins the default, helper argument vector, and live acquire/release call sites. **Not changed:** no renewal process, no blocking packet validator, no scheduler/publish-mode behavior, no Rust/Cargo/workflow/schema behavior. **Verification:** focused `AutonomousCodexExecutorDryRun.Tests.ps1` Pester 12/12; full `tools/dispatch-tests` Pester 392/392; touched-file PSScriptAnalyzer 0 findings (full-repo analyzer still reports the pre-existing `Install-Windows11-D-Standalone.ps1:94` warning); `git diff --check` clean; `.ai/dispatch.verify.ps1` exit 0.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (ADR-121 queue handoff claim lifecycle): `Invoke-AiDispatchQueue.ps1` now acquires an ADR-121 handoff claim by default after isolated worktree creation and before `Invoke-AiDispatchLoop.ps1` starts. The live lock is shared through the primary checkout at `.ai/handoff-claims/<DISPATCH_ID>/claim.json`, while append-only claim events are written under the isolated worktree's `ai_handoffs/claims/*.json` path so normal queue staging can publish them. A competing live claim blocks before execution, removes the empty just-created worktree and fresh branch, and leaves no run-dir copy-out obligation because the loop never ran. Successful runs release the claim after the loop exits and before dispatch-log generation/staging. `-SkipHandoffClaim` is an operator escape hatch; default queue, auto, and scheduler-invoked queue runs keep the claim lifecycle enabled. `AI_DISPATCH_AUTOMATION.md` and ADR-121 now document the live behavior, and source-level queue tests pin claim acquisition after worktree creation, release before dispatch-log/staging, and the pre-loop cleanup exemption in the existing worktree/log invariants. **Not changed:** no blocking packet validator, no loop executor behavior, no guard behavior, no scheduler registration or publish-mode semantics, no Rust/Cargo/workflow/schema behavior. **Verification:** focused Pester (`Issue231-DispatchLogPathStableAfterCleanup`, `Issue259-RunEvidenceCopyOut`, `AutonomousCodexExecutorDryRun`) 29/29; full `tools/dispatch-tests` Pester 390/390; PSScriptAnalyzer 0 findings; `git diff --check` clean; `.ai/dispatch.verify.ps1` exit 0.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (ADR-121 split live-lock/event roots): `Invoke-HandoffClaim.ps1` now supports a separate `-LiveRoot` / `LiveRepoRoot` for the mutable live lock while preserving `-Root` / `RepoRoot` as the append-only claim-event location. Default behavior is unchanged: without `-LiveRoot`, live lock and event JSON both stay under the same root. This prepares real queue/worktree integration: a future queue runner can place `.ai/handoff-claims/<DISPATCH_ID>/claim.json` in the shared primary checkout while writing `ai_handoffs/claims/*.json` under the isolated worktree that will be committed. `tools/dispatch-tests/HandoffClaim.Tests.ps1` adds a two-worktree split-root test proving the first worktree writes the event locally, the primary root carries the live lock, and a second worktree sharing that live root is blocked without writing its own event. **Not changed:** no dispatch loop/queue/auto claim acquisition, no queue argument plumbing, no runner renewal/release lifecycle, no scope guard behavior beyond the prior slice, no blocking validator, no scheduler/publish behavior, no Rust/Cargo/workflow behavior. **Verification:** focused `HandoffClaim.Tests.ps1` Pester 9/9; full `tools/dispatch-tests` Pester 387/387; PSScriptAnalyzer 0 findings; `git diff --check` clean; `.ai/dispatch.verify.ps1` exit 0.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (ADR-121 claim-event queue scope allowance): the queue scope guard now treats helper-generated ADR-121 claim event JSON for the active dispatch as protocol artifacts, so a future runner claim can be staged without tripping the pre-`git add -A` guard. `Invoke-AiDispatchQueue.ps1` adds a narrow `Test-HandoffClaimEventPath` matcher for `ai_handoffs/claims/<DISPATCH_ID>_<TIMESTAMP>_<claim|renew|release|expire|reclaim>.json` and wires it beside the existing direct-packet artifact allowance. The matcher remains dispatch-id-specific, event-name-specific, timestamp-shape-specific, and JSON-only; arbitrary nested `ai_handoffs/**` paths remain rejected. `tools/dispatch-tests/Issue237-DotfileScopeGuard.Tests.ps1` now covers both the accepted claim-event path and a rejected non-claim nested handoff path against a temp git worktree. ADR-121 records this staging-prep slice. **Not changed:** no `Invoke-HandoffClaim.ps1` behavior, no dispatch loop/queue/auto claim acquisition, no claim renewal/release lifecycle in runners, no blocking validator, no scheduler/publish behavior, no Rust/Cargo/workflow behavior. **Verification:** focused `Issue237-DotfileScopeGuard.Tests.ps1` Pester 34/34; full `tools/dispatch-tests` Pester 386/386; PSScriptAnalyzer 0 findings; `git diff --check` clean; `.ai/dispatch.verify.ps1` exit 0.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (ADR-121 optional TASK envelope guidance): new TASK packets can now carry the optional ADR-121 machine-readable scope envelope without changing queue behavior. `ai_handoffs/templates/TASK_PACKET.md` adds an "Advisory machine-readable scope envelope" section after the human-readable scope lists, with a marker-delimited `<!-- handoff:envelope v1 -->` block, `MAY_EDIT`, `MUST_NOT_EDIT`, and `INCIDENTAL_OK: false` defaults. `Invoke-AiDispatchLoop.ps1`'s Planner prompt now tells Codex to mirror `### MAY edit` / `### MAY add new files` into `MAY_EDIT`, mirror `### MUST NOT edit` / `### MUST NOT add new files` into `MUST_NOT_EDIT`, avoid Markdown backticks and brace expansion inside the envelope, and delete or leave the block empty for read-only/unsafe-to-express scopes so advisory validation reports `UNCHECKED`. ADR-121 records this template slice. `tools/dispatch-tests/Invoke-PlanFill-Prompt.Tests.ps1` now covers both prompt guidance and template markers. **Not changed:** no queue scope-guard parser behavior, no blocking handoff gate, no runner claim/lock integration, no scheduler/publish behavior, no Rust/Cargo/workflow behavior. **Verification:** focused `Invoke-PlanFill-Prompt.Tests.ps1` Pester 10/10; full `tools/dispatch-tests` Pester 384/384; PSScriptAnalyzer 0 findings; `git diff --check` clean; `.ai/dispatch.verify.ps1` exit 0.

> Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (ADR-121 advisory verify integration): ADR-121's third implementation slice is now wired into the canonical verify path as advisory-only output. `.ai/dispatch.verify.ps1` runs the existing `Test-HandoffPacket.ps1` after the CI-parity steps as a non-counted advisory section, discovers dispatch context from `RGE_AI_DISPATCH_ID` or an `ai-dispatch/<id>` branch, validates the latest `EXEC` packet when present (falling back to `TASK`), passes the matching `TASK` packet for optional scope validation, and includes Planner-owned `CORRECT` packets as override authorities. The hook prints `HANDOFF_ADVISORY: SKIP|PASS|WARN`, never uses `-Blocking`, and does not change the verify gate's exit code or step count. `Invoke-AiDispatchLoop.ps1` now sets and restores `RGE_AI_DISPATCH_ID` / `RGE_AI_DISPATCH_ROUND` only around the verification child process so standalone loop runs have the same advisory context as queue branch runs. `Test-HandoffPacket.ps1` and ADR-121 prose now describe the advisory integration state. > Snapshot: 2026-06-06 (ADR-121 claim/lock helper): the second ADR-121 mechanism now has standalone advisory tooling. New `Invoke-HandoffClaim.ps1` supports `Status`, `Claim`, `Renew`, `Release`, and `Reclaim` for dispatch IDs, using atomic live lock-directory creation under `.ai/handoff-claims/<DISPATCH_ID>/` and durable append-only claim events under `ai_handoffs/claims/*.json`. It validates dispatch IDs to prevent path escape, records actor/harness/branch/timestamp/TTL, blocks other actors while a claim is live, permits renew/release only by the owning actor+harness, treats expired claims as `STALE` until explicit `Reclaim`, writes `expire` + `reclaim` events for stale takeovers, and offers `-Blocking` for callers that want `BLOCKED`/`STALE` to exit 2. New `tools/dispatch-tests/HandoffClaim.Tests.ps1` covers available status, claim creation/event JSON, duplicate actor blocking, same-owner `OWNED`, renew ownership, release ownership/removal, stale explicit reclaim, and dispatch-id path safety. **Not changed:** no dispatch loop/queue/auto/guard integration, no `.ai/dispatch.verify.ps1` integration, no packet templates, scheduler, schema/workflow, or blocking gate. **Verification:** focused claim Pester 8/8; full `tools/dispatch-tests` Pester 374/374; PSScriptAnalyzer 0 findings; `.ai/dispatch.verify.ps1` exit 0.

> AI Handoff Protocol: AI-to-AI dispatch packets (Planner / Executor / Reviewer with human arbitration) follow the append-only governance protocol in [`ai_handoffs/AI_HANDOFF_PROTOCOL.md`](ai_handoffs/AI_HANDOFF_PROTOCOL.md). Templates: [`ai_handoffs/templates/`](ai_handoffs/templates/). The protocol is now also runtime-automated: `Invoke-AiDispatchLoop.ps1` orchestrates one bounded dispatch (Codex plans / Claude executes / Codex controls, with Claude's `GATE_VERDICT` plan-gate marker and `EXEC_STATUS` / `EXEC_PACKET` execute markers driving control flow), and `Invoke-AiDispatchQueue.ps1` is the GitHub issue queue runner — it pulls the oldest open `ai-dispatch`-labelled issue, runs it through the loop on a per-issue `ai-dispatch/ISSUE-<n>` branch, writes a timestamped `ai_dispatch_logs/log_*.md` audit file, and auto-publishes only when the loop exits 0 and Codex control says `pass`; failed or blocked runs remain local and are labelled failed. The recurring `/loop` queue cadence is semi-attended and bound to the local authenticated CLI session, not a headless cloud daemon. See [`AI_DISPATCH_AUTOMATION.md`](AI_DISPATCH_AUTOMATION.md).

> Snapshot: 2026-05-13 (Phase 7 D-Fillet real round geometry chapter sub-epsilon — **multi-edge corner blending, IMPLEMENTED**): closes the last ADR-119 D8 sub-dispatch after sub-zeta. `RoundFilletOp::evaluate` now defers face-strip substitution across the full selected-spec set, records candidate insets per `(TopologyFaceId, original vertex)`, resolves shared face-vertex collisions to one face-corner inset, and appends nameless `TopologyFaceId::DEGENERATE` corner-patch fan geometry for upstream vertices touched by 2+ selected `TwoEndpoint` / open `Path` specs. This lifts the old "corner-sharing is visually weird but topologically valid" posture while preserving the v0 identity boundary: no `BRepFaceId` for caps/corner patches, no analytic/G2 torus patch, no variable-radius/setback solver, no `RoundFilletSpec` / `RoundFilletPathSpec` shape change, no `RoundFilletError` variant, no resolver/chamfer/Cargo change, no new ADR/lint/doctrine. Coverage added across all four upstream families: Cuboid two corner-sharing edges (pins the shared NegZ corner inset at `[-0.4, -0.4, -0.5]`), Extrude bottom-perimeter + vertical-seam, Loft bottom-perimeter + vertical-seam, and Revolve mixed cap-side `TwoEndpoint` + side-side `Path`. Files modified: `crates/cad-core/src/operators/round_fillet/mod.rs` plus corner-branch tests in `cuboid.rs`, `extrude.rs`, `loft.rs`, and `revolve.rs`; docs updated in `Status.md`, `HANDOFF.md`, and `change.md`. **Verification gates ALL GREEN**: `cargo +nightly fmt --check -p rge-cad-core` exit 0; `git diff --check` exit 0; `cargo build -p rge-cad-core` exit 0; `cargo test -p rge-cad-core --lib --no-fail-fast` = **471 passed / 0 failed / 0 ignored** (+4 from sub-zeta); `cargo test --workspace --no-fail-fast` exit 0 = **2546 passed / 0 failed / 19 ignored** (+4 net from 2542); `cargo run -q -p rge-tool-architecture-lints -- all` exit 0 (9 enforcement + 1 supplementary PASS). **D-Fillet chapter status**: sub-alpha + sub-beta + sub-gamma + sub-beta.gamma + sub-delta.revisit + sub-beta.gamma-extend + sub-zeta Commit 1 + sub-zeta Commit 2 + sub-epsilon all CLOSED; ADR-119 D1-D8 complete. Future pressure remains output identity for new surfaces, analytic/continuous corner patches, variable radius/setbacks, or CAD-kernel backing.

> Snapshot: 2026-05-13 (Phase 7 D-Fillet real round geometry chapter sub-ζ — **general circular-path Revolve via 2-commit staging: Commit 1 inert RoundFilletSpecKind enum-wrapper refactor (`1052a3d`) + Commit 2 RoundFilletPathSpec + Revolve circular-path side-side acceptance, IMPLEMENTED**): introduces `pub(crate) enum RoundFilletSpecKind { TwoEndpoint(RoundFilletSpec), Path(RoundFilletPathSpec) }` + multi-segment swept-cylinder Path branch in `RoundFilletOp::evaluate` + lifts Revolve full-mode AND partial-mode side-side rejections to Path-spec acceptance. **Completes Revolve coverage** — all `N` full-mode edges (closed loops) + all `3N` partial-mode edges (cap-perimeter + cap-side + side-side open arcs) now accept under the round-fillet substrate. **2-commit staging (per Codex execution-order confirmation + user direction "Then proceed")**: **Commit 1 inert wrapper (`1052a3d`)**: introduces `RoundFilletSpecKind` with ONE variant `TwoEndpoint(RoundFilletSpec)` (Path variant deferred to Commit 2 so Rust's exhaustive-match forces the Commit 2 arm explicitly), changes `RoundFilletUpstream::resolve_round_spec` return type + `RoundFilletOp::round_specs` element type to the wrapper, wraps all 9 per-upstream `Ok(RoundFilletSpec { ... })` returns in `::TwoEndpoint(...)`, adds `#[cfg(test)] expect_two_endpoint()` accessor, updates ~25 test direct-call sites with `let spec = spec.expect_two_endpoint();` shadow-bind. **Inert gate passes**: workspace stays at `2534 / 0 / 19` exact (pre-Commit-1 == post-Commit-1; load-bearing inert proof). **Commit 2 shipping (this entry; about-to-commit)**: adds `RoundFilletPathSpec` struct + `::Path(RoundFilletPathSpec)` variant + Path branch in `RoundFilletOp::evaluate` (~140 LoC inside the match arm) + `revolve_side_side_path_spec` helper in revolve.rs + 3 reject-test flips + 2 trailing-assertion flips + 8 new Path-branch tests. **Per user direction at full-plan green-light**: "Then proceed" — covered the 2-commit plan. Executed exactly that scope; zero halt-condition triggers. **Path spec geometric model**: For each path-ring r along the seam, position `pos_r = r * N + (i+1)%N`, with per-ring inward directions `path_face_a_inwards[r]` (rotated Side(i) outward normal around Y-axis to θ_r) and `path_face_b_inwards[r]` (similarly for Side((i+1)%N)). Edge tangent at ring r is the swept tangent `(-sin(θ_r), 0, cos(θ_r))`. The dihedral angle along the path is CONSTANT (equals the profile's interior polygon angle at the shared vertex), but the inward DIRECTIONS rotate around Y-axis with θ — hence per-ring storage. For partial mode `θ_r = r * angle / segments`, M+1 ring positions, `closed_loop = false`. For full mode `θ_r = r * 2π / segments`, M = segments ring positions (no separate closing ring; index wraps via `(r+1) % M`), `closed_loop = true`. **Path branch in `RoundFilletOp::evaluate`** (~140 new LoC inside the match arm): for each ring, run sub-β.γ general-dihedral math (inset scale + axis_center + cross-section vertices); face-strip multi-ring substitution scans Side(i) and Side((i+1)%N) triangles for path-vertex occurrences and substitutes inset indices keyed by ring; cylinder cross-section stitching connects ring r to ring r+1 (or wraps r=M-1 to r=0 for closed loops) with 2N triangles per ring-step. Per-edge contribution: 2*(M+1) inset verts + (N+1)*(M+1) cross-section verts + 2*M*N cylinder triangles for partial; 2*M + (N+1)*M + 2*M*N for full. **Revolve side-side rejection lift**: `revolve.rs::resolve_round_spec` partial mode `[0, N)` and full mode all edges now route to `revolve_side_side_path_spec(...)` returning `::Path(RoundFilletPathSpec)`; previously both rejected with `UnsupportedEdgeGeometry`. **Three reject-test flips + 2 trailing-assertion flips** (deliberate boundary-shift bookkeeping mirroring sub-β.γ-extend's 3 reject-test flips at `978f507`): `new_for_revolve_full_mode_all_edges_unsupported` → `new_for_revolve_full_mode_all_edges_accept_as_closed_loop_path`; `new_for_revolve_partial_mode_side_side_unsupported` → `new_for_revolve_partial_mode_side_side_accepts_as_open_arc_path`; `new_for_revolve_partial_mode_mixed_selection_rejects_first_unsupported` → `new_for_revolve_partial_mode_mixed_selection_accepts_post_sub_zeta`. Plus 2 trailing-assertion flips inside `resolve_round_spec_face_ids_match_canonical_emission_order` (canonical 2 Err → Path accept with face IDs) and `resolve_round_spec_inward_vectors_unit_and_perpendicular_for_cap_side`'s side-side loop (`is_err()` → Path accept + unit-length per-ring check). **Eight new Path-branch tests** pinning sub-ζ Commit 2 invariants: `evaluate_one_partial_side_side_edge_produces_expected_counts` (load-bearing — proves Path branch runs end-to-end; +99v/+128t for ring profile, segments=8, angle=π/2); `evaluate_one_full_mode_side_side_edge_produces_expected_counts_closed_loop` (full-mode +88v/+128t — closed-loop wrap); `resolve_round_spec_partial_side_side_path_face_ids` (Side(i) ∩ Side((i+1)%N) with wrap at last edge); `resolve_round_spec_full_mode_side_side_path_is_closed_loop_with_segments_rings` (closed_loop=true; M=segments rings); **`resolve_round_spec_square_partial_side_side_yields_90_degree_dihedral_per_ring` — load-bearing regression** (square profile interior=90°, every ring's `a·b ≈ 0`); **`resolve_round_spec_pentagon_partial_side_side_yields_consistent_dihedral_per_ring` — load-bearing non-90° proof + dihedral-constancy** (pentagon interior is non-90°; verifies the constant-dihedral-along-path invariant — combined with sub-δ.revisit Loft 45° + sub-β.γ-extend Extrude pentagon 108°, the chapter now has THREE non-90° proof-points spanning BOTH the TwoEndpoint AND Path branches); `resolve_round_spec_partial_side_side_path_vertices_match_revolve_layout` (square segments=8: M+1=9 path vertices `[1, 5, 9, ..., 33]`); `resolve_round_spec_full_mode_side_side_path_vertices_match_full_path_layout` (square segments=8 full: M=8 path vertices `[1, 5, 9, ..., 29]`). **Substrate posture**: `RoundFilletOp` struct + `RoundFilletSpec` struct + `RoundFilletError` enum + `RoundFilletUpstream` trait signature byte-identical from sub-ζ Commit 1 `1052a3d` (only `RoundFilletSpecKind` enum grew the `Path` variant + `RoundFilletOp::evaluate`'s match arm grew the `Path` body); > Snapshot: 2026-05-12 (W04 follow-on **raw Winch hot-reload measurement, IMPLEMENTED**): closes the empirical question raised at sub-β open ("does Winch meaningfully improve swap-window / hot-reload p95 enough to matter for fast-iteration scenarios?"). **Answer: NO — Winch does NOT meaningfully improve hot-reload p95 for the `script_host_counter` orchestrated workload.** Measured 2026-05-12 (release-mode, recorder host): Winch p95 = **0.865 ms** vs Cranelift's re-validated 0.818 ms = **1.057× ratio — within ±6% noise band**. Both pass PLAN §5.6 <100 ms gate by >100× margin (Winch at 0.9% of budget, Cranelift at 0.8%). **Mechanical explanation cross-referencing sub-α/β analysis**: Winch's compile-path advantage (~25% faster cold-start measured at sub-β: 0.305 ms vs Cranelift 0.405 ms) balances against Winch's runtime-path penalty (3.57× slower script_tick_1m: 2.547 ns/op vs Cranelift 0.713 ns/op) — neither dominates for this workload, giving near-identical hot-reload p95. **No engine-default change proposed**; `rge-runtime-wasmtime-engine::Engine::new` continues to use `cranelift_opt_level(OptLevel::Speed)` (production hot-reload stays on Cranelift); Winch measurement is a BASELINE.md release-readiness data point. **Per user direction** at dispatch open: "Reuse the existing hot-reload benchmark shape if possible. Halt if hot-reload harness is tightly coupled to script_host_counter orchestration and cannot isolate raw Winch without a broader harness rewrite." > Snapshot: 2026-05-12 (Phase 3.4 W04 cross-engine bench comparison **sub-β: raw WasmtimeSinglepass / Winch column closed, IMPLEMENTED**): closes the second W04 column with measured numbers. All four `_pending W04 sub-β_` cells (`script_tick_1m_iters` / `per_frame_tick_10k_entities` / `cold_start` / `memory_overhead`) flipped to measured numbers via NEW `crates/script-bench/src/wasmtime_singlepass.rs` fixture (~330L mirror of sub-α with one config-strategy swap: `Config::strategy(Strategy::Winch)` instead of `cranelift_opt_level(OptLevel::Speed)`). **Per user direction** "Scope it as four measured rows, baseline/log updates, and a minimal engine-config path only. Stop if Winch/singlepass support is not available on the recorder host or if runtime config plumbing wants a broader `Engine` reshape than expected. Keep `script_host_counter` and raw wasmtime columns sharply separated." This dispatch executes exactly that scope. **Config plumbing**: `winch` feature flag added to `crates/script-bench/Cargo.toml`'s `wasmtime` dep declaration ONLY (script-bench-local override; Cargo feature unification compiles wasmtime once with `["cranelift", "runtime", "std", "winch"]`); the runtime crates (`rge-runtime-wasmtime` / `rge-runtime-wasmtime-engine` / `rge-script-host`) STAY on their default-Cranelift-only path — no workspace-root `Cargo.toml` change, no broader `Engine` reshape. **Three sub-α WAT consts promoted from `const` → `pub(crate) const`** (`SCRIPT_TICK_1M_WAT` / `PER_FRAME_TICK_10K_WAT` / `COLD_START_EMPTY_WAT`) so sub-β can re-import them via `use crate::wasmtime_cranelift::{...}` — single-source WAT fixtures, no duplication. **Measurement results (release-mode, recorder host)**: `script_tick_1m_iters` raw Winch = 2.547 ns/op (**3.77× native; FAILS 1.5×**; 3.57× over Cranelift — Winch's non-optimizing codegen costs significantly on tight compute loops, validating Cranelift's register-allocation + loop-hoisting + dead-code-elimination); `per_frame_tick_10k_entities` raw Winch = 9.750 ns/entity (**12.83× native; FAILS 1.5×**; **only 1.28× over Cranelift** — the central finding); `cold_start` raw Winch = 0.305 ms (**PASS < 50ms; 0.75× of Cranelift — Winch FASTER at compile**, validating Winch's design point: fast compile, slower runtime); `memory_overhead` raw Winch = 13 680 B / module (**1.000× of Cranelift** — empty-module AOT artifact size is compiler-independent for this fixture). **Central question answered (sub-β's load-bearing finding)**: per user direction "is the raw per-entity overhead a Cranelift-specific shape or a broader direct-WASM execution cost?" → **the per-entity overhead is BROADLY characteristic of direct-WASM execution, NOT Cranelift-specific**. `per_frame_tick_10k_entities` ratios: Cranelift 10.034× / Winch 12.829× over native; Winch/Cranelift ratio is only 1.28× — both compilers land in the same order-of-magnitude penalty band. If the 10× ratio were Cranelift-specific (e.g., a missed bounds-check elision opportunity), Winch — the simpler / less-optimizing compiler — would show a MUCH larger gap. Instead, the tight cross-compiler ratio means the per-entity penalty is driven by the **WASM execution model itself** (bounds-checked linear-memory access on every f32 load/store, per-element instruction overhead, no auto-vectorization). **The PLAN §5.6 1.5× target is structurally unachievable for any direct-WASM per-entity-loop workload regardless of compiler choice**; the `script_host_counter_bulk` pattern (single host crossing per frame, host iterates entities natively) is the architectural answer, validated by the 1.34× ratio it achieves. This is "uncomfortable data" per user framing — recorded honestly. **Cranelift-vs-Winch cross-compiler analysis recorded in BASELINE.md** with engineering takeaway: Cranelift is the better choice for compute-bound + memory-access-heavy hot paths; Winch is the better choice for hot-reload / fast-iteration paths. The script-host's hot-reload uses Cranelift (cranelift_opt_level Speed) — correct for runtime perf; Winch would save cold-start at the cost of swap-window p95 (0.818 ms on Cranelift). **No engine-default change proposed**. **HARD NON-GOALS observed**: NO workspace-root `Cargo.toml` change (feature flag in `crates/script-bench/Cargo.toml` only; runtime crates unchanged); NO `crates/runtime-wasmtime-engine/**` change; NO `crates/runtime-wasmtime/**` change; NO `crates/script-host/**` change (script_host_counter rows preserved verbatim; sharply separated from raw wasmtime columns per user direction); NO MLua / Wasmer / BevyExtism deps; NO PLAN §5.6 1.5× target retarget; NO native-baseline rewrite; NO `engine_stub.rs` deletion; NO Cranelift-side change beyond the 3-keyword `const → pub(crate) const` promotion of WAT fixtures (sub-α tests + numbers + struct + impl byte-identical); NO architecture change anywhere; NO new ADR / new lint / new exemption / new doctrine doc / new §18 companion; NO `unsafe`; NO `plans/IMPLEMENTATION.md` change (Phase 3.4 exit criteria all already CLOSED in `06eb23a`; W04 work is benchmark-breadth, NOT Phase 3.4 closure); NO `#[ignore]`-marked tests (mirrors sub-α + phase_3_3 / phase_3_4 NOT-ignored pattern); NO raw Winch hot-reload measurement (sub-β scope was 4 raw fixtures only; the raw cranelift hot-reload row likewise stays unmeasured per sub-α scope). **Verification gates ALL GREEN**: `cargo +nightly fmt --check -p rge-script-bench` exit 0 (no fmt fixups needed); `cargo build -p rge-script-bench --release` clean (1m 27s — first compile pulled in `wasmtime-internal-winch v44.0.1` + `winch-codegen v44.0.1` + rebuild of `wasmtime` + `cranelift-codegen` to integrate Winch; > Snapshot: 2026-05-12 (Phase 6 pass-record-integration **sub-β: production depth wire, IMPLEMENTED**): production `editor-shell::render_path` now consumes the frame-graph transient-texture substrate end-to-end — `TexturePool` + `BufferPool` + `CompiledFrameGraph` constructed at `init_render_state`, `build_resource_map` drives per-frame transient depth-texture acquisition via the dispatch-122 builder discipline (no direct `TexturePool::acquire` from the pass-record site, preserving ADR-118 L213's load-bearing lifetime rule), `Some(&depth_view)` flows through the inline `RenderPassDepthStencilAttachment` literal at `render_frame`, and the shared `LitMeshPipeline` is constructed via the sub-α `new_with_depth(Some(DepthStateKey::new(Depth24Plus, false, LessEqual)))` path. **Honest scope** (per user direction): this dispatch consumes the transient substrate and prevents a depth-state regression that adding a populated depth buffer would otherwise introduce, but does NOT prove a user-visible Z-fight fix — that claim requires sub-γ measurement or a visual harness, neither of which exists yet. **Pre-dispatch inspection-first verdict**: substrate-disciplined path (`FrameGraph` + `ResourceMap`) is workable but heavy for one transient resource (3 new state fields on `EditorShell` + per-frame builder-layer ceremony); direct `TexturePool::acquire` would be cleaner but is explicitly forbidden by dispatch-122 substrate-discipline rule. Per user guardrail, the heavy path is the only option — bypassing creates a "second resource lifetime path" inconsistent with the substrate design. **Substrate consumption flow (per dispatch-122 recipe)**: `init_render_state` constructs `TexturePool::new()` + `BufferPool::new()` (the latter unused but required by `build_resource_map`'s signature; future transient-buffer consumers populate `map.buffer_map` from the same builder pass with no further plumbing churn), builds a single-pass `FrameGraph` declaring one write of `DEPTH_RESOURCE_ID` at format `Depth24Plus`, compiles, stores; `render_frame` opens with `tex_pool.begin_frame() + buf_pool.begin_frame()` (ADR-118 D4 ring rotation), `build_resource_map(compiled, device, &mut tex_pool, &mut buf_pool)`, extracts `Arc::clone(map.texture_map.get(&DEPTH_RESOURCE_ID).expect(...))`, creates depth view, then proceeds with the existing inline render-pass body — the only delta is `depth_stencil_attachment: Some(RenderPassDepthStencilAttachment { view: &depth_view, depth_ops: Some(Operations { load: Clear(1.0), store: Store }), stencil_ops: None })` literal inline (NO refactor of the inline render pass into a `record_lit_mesh_pass(...)` call per user direction "Do not refactor the whole inline render pass into the helper unless it is the smallest way to pass depth cleanly"); `resize_render_path` rebuilds `compiled_frame_graph` against the new surface dimensions because `TextureDescriptor` is keyed on width/height and the descriptor flows verbatim into `TexturePool`'s free-list identity. **Depth-state choice** (`LessEqual` + `depth_write_enabled: false`) per user direction "Keep depth format tied to the acquired texture format and `LessEqual`, `depth_write_enabled: false` per the existing future note": both the cuboid draw and the highlight-overlay draw share the single `LitMeshPipeline`; with `depth_write_enabled: false` on both, the depth buffer stays at `Clear(1.0)` for the entire frame and every fragment passes `LessEqual` against 1.0 — depth is functionally a no-op for the cuboid + overlay, matching pre-sub-β no-depth visual behavior exactly. **Borrow-flow design**: `render_frame` does the pool work in a scoped block FIRST (`&mut self.texture_pool` + `&mut self.buffer_pool` + immutable borrow of `self.gfx_ctx` via `gfx_ctx.device()`; all on distinct fields, accepted by Rust's borrow checker via struct-field-level borrow splitting) before re-acquiring the existing immutable borrows on neighbouring state — keeps borrow lifetimes non-overlapping without `RefCell` / `Mutex`. `build_resource_map` failure path mirrors the existing `get_current_texture` failure handling: warn + `window.request_redraw()` + return `true` (skip frame, recoverable on next tick). The `expect(...)` on `map.texture_map.get(&DEPTH_RESOURCE_ID)` is justified because a well-formed single-pass `FrameGraph::compile` guarantees descriptor presence — `MissingDescriptorForGroup` cannot arise for the construction produced by `build_lit_mesh_compiled_frame_graph`. **Acceptable bounded leak on resize**: when surface size changes, the new `CompiledFrameGraph` carries a new `TextureDescriptor`; old textures keyed on the previous descriptor drain through the ring rotation and accumulate in `free_lists` as stale entries (bounded by `FRAMES_IN_FLIGHT=2` allocations per resize event). Acceptable for v0; pool-level free-list pruning is out of scope (would surface as a substrate-level dispatch if scale pressure demands). **New EditorShell state fields** (3 total, all `Option<T>`): `texture_pool: Option<TexturePool>` / `buffer_pool: Option<BufferPool>` / `compiled_frame_graph: Option<CompiledFrameGraph>`. Initialized to `None` in both `EditorShell::new` (delegates to `with_world`) and `EditorShell::with_world`. **New constants** in `render_path.rs`: `DEPTH_FORMAT: wgpu::TextureFormat = Depth24Plus`; `DEPTH_RESOURCE_ID: ResourceId = ResourceId::from_bytes([b'r', b'g', b'e', b'.', b'e', b'd', b's', b'h', b'.', b'd', b'e', b'p', b't', b'h', 0, 1])` (ASCII prefix informational; opaque-ness preserved per `ResourceId` contract); `build_lit_mesh_compiled_frame_graph(surface_width, surface_height) -> CompiledFrameGraph` helper (single-pass graph with one depth-texture write at given dims); `lit_mesh_depth_state() -> DepthStateKey` (`Depth24Plus, depth_write_enabled: false, LessEqual`). **HARD NON-GOALS observed**: NO change to `crates/gfx/src/**` (substrate complete; sub-α landed the consumer API; NO Gate A marker update at `plans/IMPLEMENTATION.md:468` / `BASELINE.md` (sub-γ scope); NO new ADR / new lint / new exemption / new doctrine doc / new §18 companion; NO pipeline splitting (single shared `LitMeshPipeline` for cuboid + overlay; one `DepthStateKey`); NO refactor of the inline render pass into a `record_lit_mesh_pass(...)` call (kept inline per user direction; smallest delta is the inline `depth_stencil_attachment` literal); NO direct `TexturePool::acquire` bypassing `FrameGraph + build_resource_map` (substrate-discipline rule preserved); > Snapshot: 2026-05-12 (Phase 7 D-Fillet **sub-ε.α: graph-level Fillet face-identity inheritance, IMPLEMENTED**): lifts the first FilletOp output-identity NON-GOAL (`crates/cad-core/src/operators/fillet/mod.rs:32`) via a graph-layer change only — no `impl BRepProvider for FilletOp`, no new face-id `KIND_FILLET` bytestring, no FilletOp source change, no FilletOp `evaluate` change, no edge-resolver change. **Substrate delta**: NEW `OperatorNode::Fillet(_)` arm in `crates/cad-core/src/topology/resolve.rs`'s `resolve_step` (~12L incl. inline rationale comment) — mirror of the pre-existing Transform arm — recurses to the unique input via the existing `single_input_node` helper and returns upstream face IDs unchanged. **The load-bearing structural observation**: `FilletOp::evaluate` (`crates/cad-core/src/operators/fillet/mod.rs:336`) clones upstream `positions`/`indices` verbatim and APPENDS chamfer-cap geometry — every upstream face exists bit-identical in the output mesh, so face-identity pass-through is unambiguously correct without any per-operator `BRepProvider` impl. > Snapshot: 2026-05-12 (Phase 6 frame-graph chapter — **dispatch 122: `ResourceMap` builder + `AliasingGroup::max_descriptor` analytical helper, IMPLEMENTED**): lands the per-frame `ResourceId → Arc<wgpu::{Texture,Buffer}>` mapping that consumes dispatches 120 (`e050e06`) + 121 (`c356f32`) and structurally enforces ADR-118's `acquire()` dedup contract. NEW `crates/gfx/src/frame_graph/resource_map.rs` (~330L total — ~50L module doc + impl + 5 unit tests). Two new public types: **`ResourceMap`** = `{ texture_map: BTreeMap<ResourceId, Arc<wgpu::Texture>>, buffer_map: BTreeMap<ResourceId, Arc<wgpu::Buffer>> }` per ADR-118 D2 (pools separate at the allocator level; class discrimination happens at the builder boundary based on each group's max descriptor); **`ResourceMapError::MissingDescriptorForGroup(AliasingGroupId)`** — diagnostic-only failure mode for partial / hand-built `CompiledFrameGraph`s. **`build_resource_map(compiled, device, &mut tex_pool, &mut buf_pool)`** iterates `CompiledFrameGraph::aliasing_groups()` exactly once, computes the max descriptor per group via the new `AliasingGroup::max_descriptor` analytical helper, calls each pool's `acquire(...)` exactly ONCE per group, then fans the returned `Arc` to every `ResourceId` member of the group. This is THE structural enforcement of ADR-118 L213's load-bearing dedup contract — no internal pool dedup is needed because the iteration discipline at the builder makes intra-group acquires impossible by construction. **`AliasingGroup::max_descriptor` helper** (~30L net delta in `compile.rs`): `filter_map(|rid| descriptors.get(rid)).max_by_key(|d| d.byte_size_estimate())` over the group's `ResourceId`s; returns `None` for empty groups or groups whose members have no descriptors registered (the precondition for `MissingDescriptorForGroup`). **Re-exports**: `frame_graph/mod.rs` adds `pub mod resource_map;` + `pub use resource_map::{ResourceMap, ResourceMapError, build_resource_map};`; `lib.rs` adds the three idents to the existing `frame_graph::` re-export block. **ADR-118 wording softening (single bullet L213)**: "Dispatch 122 — `FrameRecorder` integration. > Snapshot: 2026-05-12 (Phase 6 frame-graph chapter — **dispatch 121: BufferPool MVP per ADR-118 D2+D3+D4+D5, IMPLEMENTED**): lands the descriptor-keyed transient-buffer pool as a clean mirror of dispatch 120's TexturePool (commit `e050e06`). NEW `crates/gfx/src/frame_graph/buffer_pool.rs` (268L total — ~50L module doc + impl + 5 unit tests). Single new public type **`BufferPool`** owning `[SlotState; 2]` ring + `current_slot: usize` (identical shape to TexturePool). Per-slot state: `free_lists: HashMap<(BufferDescriptor, AliasingGroupId), Vec<Arc<wgpu::Buffer>>>` (keyed per ADR-118 D3) + `active: Vec<(BufferDescriptor, AliasingGroupId, Arc<wgpu::Buffer>)>` (flat triple — descriptor carried alongside Arc because wgpu 29's `Buffer` doesn't expose original descriptor for free-list routing at slot reset; identical rationale to TexturePool). **Three public methods**: `new()` / `default()` start at slot 0; `begin_frame()` advances `current_slot = (current_slot + 1) % FRAMES_IN_FLIGHT` then drains the new slot's `active` back into its `free_lists` (D4 ring rotation); `acquire(device, descriptor, group)` peeks the free-list via `get_mut + pop`, fallback `device.create_buffer(...)` via internal `allocate_buffer` helper, then pushes the triple into `active` and returns the `Arc<wgpu::Buffer>`. **`allocate_buffer` helper** translates `BufferDescriptor` → `wgpu::BufferDescriptor` (label = None per D1; size = `descriptor.size_bytes`; usage = `descriptor.usage`; `mapped_at_creation = false` per D1 — transient resources never CPU-map at creation). **`AliasingGroupId` REUSED via `use super::texture_pool::AliasingGroupId;`** (graph-time identity shared across both pool kinds; ADR-118 D2 separates pool *types*, not *identities*; NO redefinition). **`FRAMES_IN_FLIGHT` duplicated as a 1-LOC const** rather than hoisted (churn of moving a 1-LOC const exceeds payoff at this dispatch's scope; both pools amend together if N changes). **`texture_pool.rs` BEHAVIORAL byte-identical** — only reference is by name via `AliasingGroupId` import. **Re-exports**: `frame_graph/mod.rs` adds `pub mod buffer_pool;` + `pub use buffer_pool::BufferPool;`; dispatch 121 — BufferPool MVP (clean mirror)"; records the dispatch-120/121 split at the moment BufferPool makes the split true. Filenames updated to `texture_pool.rs` / `buffer_pool.rs` from `allocator.rs` placeholder. Not scope creep. **Tests (+5 net; workspace 2403 → 2408, exact target)**: BP-1 structural verifies empty-start + 0→1→0→1 rotation across 3 `begin_frame` calls; BP-2 GPU-gated confirms `acquire` returns Arc with `strong_count=2`; BP-3 GPU-gated — the load-bearing free-list-reuse proof via `Arc::as_ptr` equality after full ring round-trip; BP-4 GPU-gated verifies distinct `AliasingGroupId`s produce distinct allocations under identical descriptor (D3 key includes group); BP-5 GPU-gated verifies distinct descriptors (size 4096 vs 8192) in same group produce distinct allocations. > Snapshot: 2026-05-12 (Phase 6 frame-graph chapter — **dispatch 119: `ResourceDescriptor` types + frame-graph descriptor flow, IMPLEMENTED**): implements ADR-118 D7's first code step. NEW `crates/gfx/src/frame_graph/descriptor.rs` (~350L incl. ~165L tests + ~50L module doc) introduces three public types: **`TextureDescriptor`** (9 wgpu-29 fields per ADR-118 D1 — `width / height / depth_or_array_layers / mip_level_count / sample_count / format / usage / dimension / view_dimension`; `label` and `mapped_at_creation` deliberately omitted per D1 to prevent pool over-fragmentation), **`BufferDescriptor`** (`size_bytes + usage` per D1), and **`ResourceClassDescriptor::{Texture(TextureDescriptor), Buffer(BufferDescriptor)}`** as the graph-time routing discriminator (pools remain separate at allocator level per D2; the enum exists purely for API uniformity through `add_pass`). All three derive `Clone + Copy + Debug + PartialEq + Eq + Hash` — `wgpu::TextureUsages` / `BufferUsages` / `TextureFormat` / `TextureDimension` / `TextureViewDimension` all derive `Hash + Eq` in wgpu-types 29 (verified via cargo cache source inspection of `wgpu-types-29.0.3/src/{buffer.rs:62, texture.rs:24/69/169, texture/format.rs:124}`), so no hand-rolled wrapping needed. Helper `byte_size_estimate()` on each descriptor + on the enum returns approximate bytes (uses `wgpu::TextureFormat::block_copy_size(None)` for textures + geometric-series 4/3 upper bound for mip pyramids) for dispatch 120's D5 "max descriptor in group" comparison. **API extension (option-(a) descriptor-on-write per dispatch brief)**: `FrameGraph::add_pass(name, reads: Vec<ResourceId>, writes: Vec<(ResourceId, ResourceClassDescriptor)>)` — writes carry descriptors; reads remain bare `ResourceId`. **Sidecar `FrameGraph::descriptors: BTreeMap<ResourceId, ResourceClassDescriptor>`** collects descriptors as `add_pass` observes writes; **deliberately kept OFF `PassNode`** to preserve content-derived `NodeId` stability under descriptor variation (two passes with the same topology but different descriptors still collide on `NodeId` per graph-foundation's content-derived identity contract). **Descriptor consistency**: `add_pass` validates `descriptors.get(rid) == new_desc` BEFORE mutating the sidecar; conflict surfaces as new `FrameGraphError::DescriptorMismatch { resource, first_decl, conflicting }`. Mid-`writes`-vector conflict leaves no partial sidecar state (validation precedes any insert — verified by dedicated test). **Compile-side**: `compile_passes(passes, descriptors)` clones the descriptor map verbatim into `CompiledFrameGraph::descriptors` (a new `#[serde(skip)]` field — wgpu types only derive serde behind a feature the workspace doesn't enable; substrate-honest given dispatch 119 ships no compiled-graph serialization path). NEW accessors `CompiledFrameGraph::descriptors() -> &BTreeMap<…>` + `descriptor(id: ResourceId) -> Option<&ResourceClassDescriptor>`. **Descriptors are NOT factored into `structural_hash`** — the analytical determinism contract remains orthogonal to descriptor metadata; two compiles with the same pass topology but different descriptors still produce equal structural hashes (verified by new test `structural_hash_orthogonal_to_descriptors`). **Optional `AliasingGroup::largest_descriptor` helper deferred** to dispatch 120 (lives next to the pool that consumes it). **`tests/frame_graph_smoke.rs` updated**: existing 3-pass `geometry / shadow / lighting` smoke now passes realistic descriptors (1920×1080 `Depth32Float` depth target, 1920×1080 `Rgba8Unorm` scene-color + lit color targets, 2048×2048 `R32Float` shadow map) and asserts the 4 descriptors round-trip through compile + recompile. NEW second smoke test `frame_graph_smoke_buffer_descriptor_round_trip` exercises a mixed buffer + texture graph (256-entry `mat4` uniform buffer feeding an `Rgba8Unorm` render target) to prove the routing enum dispatches correctly across variants. **Test deltas (workspace 2374 → 2398, +24 net)**: 16 unit tests in `descriptor.rs` (TD-1 per-field distinct checks for both descriptor types covering `width` / `format` / `view_dimension` / `size_bytes` / `usage`; TD-2 `ResourceClassDescriptor` clone+eq for both variants + cross-variant distinctness + `From` impls; byte-size estimate baseline + mip-chain 4/3 factor + buffer trivial + dispatch enum); 3 new tests in `compile.rs` (FG-D1 round-trip; mixed texture+buffer; structural-hash orthogonality); 4 new tests in `mod.rs` (FG-D1 add-pass-with-descriptors-compiles; FG-D2 conflicting-descriptor → `DescriptorMismatch` with full payload assertion; matching-descriptor accepted; mid-vector conflict leaves no partial state); 1 new smoke for buffer-descriptor round-trip. **Verification gates ALL GREEN**: `cargo +nightly fmt -p rge-gfx` exit 0; `cargo build -p rge-gfx --manifest-path A:\RCAD\RGE\Cargo.toml` clean (0 errors / 0 new warnings, 2.37s); `cargo test -p rge-gfx --manifest-path A:\RCAD\RGE\Cargo.toml` ALL PASS (156 unit + 19 integration); `cargo test --workspace --no-fail-fast --manifest-path A:\RCAD\RGE\Cargo.toml` = **2398 passed / 0 failed / 19 ignored** (was 2374; > Snapshot: 2026-05-12 (Phase 6 frame-graph chapter — **ADR-118 transient-resource allocator policy pinned**, docs-only design dispatch): authors `docs/adr/ADR-118-frame-graph-transient-resource-allocator.md` (237L) — sibling design ADR to ADR-117 for the Phase 6 chapter. ADR-117 closed the sim → render boundary semantics for §6.3 Gate C; ADR-118 closes the renderer-side transient-resource allocator semantics for §6.1 frame-graph. The analytical frame-graph substrate (`crates/gfx/src/frame_graph/{mod,pass,resource,compile}.rs`) shipped 2026-05-11 with the `# NON-GOALS` declaration deliberately deferring "GPU resource allocation" to a later dispatch; ADR-118 closes that deferral semantics-first. **7 sub-decisions pinned**: D1 — concrete `TextureDescriptor` + `BufferDescriptor` field shapes mirroring wgpu 29 (width/height/depth_or_array_layers/mip_level_count/sample_count/format/usage/dimension/view_dimension on textures; size_bytes + usage on buffers; `label` omitted to prevent over-fragmentation, `mapped_at_creation` omitted as staging-buffer concern); D2 — **separate** texture/buffer descriptor types (NOT unified `ResourceDescriptor { Texture(...), Buffer(...) }` enum) so pools are distinct and match-arm proliferation does not propagate; D3 — pool key is `(Descriptor, AliasingGroupId)` (NOT descriptor-only, NOT descriptor+frame-index) so the analytical `AliasingGroup` from `compile.rs` is the reuse contract; D4 — **ring-buffered N frames-in-flight, initial N=2** lifetime policy (NOT per-frame reset, NOT LRU, NOT explicit-release) — directly realizes "TexturePool / BufferPool keyed on frame index so allocator pressure stabilises" from `GFX_RENDER_TIER.md:234`; D5 — greedy `AliasingGroup → physical mapping` using the largest descriptor in each group (NOT lazy, NOT eager union-allocation); D6 — **trust wgpu's auto-tracked hazard barriers** (NOT manual barrier emission) — empirical amendment trigger is profiling on the 60fps simple-scene gate; D7 — **dispatch 119 = `ResourceDescriptor` types + descriptor-flow through `add_pass` / `compile`** (smallest first; ~150-250 LOC; no `Cargo.toml` change; ~3 new tests). **9 alternatives tabulated** with reasons-rejected (unified enum, descriptor-only key, per-frame reset, LRU eviction, eager union-allocation, manual barriers, explicit-release, dispatch 119 alternatives b/c/d). **10 explicit non-decisions enumerated**: cross-thread allocator (defers to renderer-thread spawn ADR — sibling to ADR-117), dynamic / persistent resources (outside lane — materials / mesh-buffers / samplers stay on existing surface), VRAM placement primitives (wgpu does not expose), shader/pipeline integration (`gfx::intent_adapter`'s lane via dispatch 121), `label` fields, `mapped_at_creation`, multi-queue scheduling, WAR / WAW tracking, external-input (swapchain) resources, free-list ordering. **Governance updates**: `docs/architecture/README.md` ADR index 9 → 10 ADRs accepted (line 124-127 paragraph updated with `118 (frame-graph transient-resource allocator policy)` entry); `docs/§18/GFX_RENDER_TIER.md` §11.1 Frame-graph entry gains single-line ADR-118 cross-ref noting allocator policy is pinned + the implementation arc (dispatches 119 / 120 / 121). **HARD NON-GOALS observed (verified empty `git diff`)**: NO `.rs` file edits anywhere in the workspace; NO `Cargo.toml` / `Cargo.lock` changes; NO `tools/architecture-lints/**` touches; NO reopening §6.2 / §6.3 / Phase 7 closures; NO new lint / no new doctrine doc / no new §18 companion doc; NO sub-ADR split (118a / 118b NOT created — single ADR holds the allocator policy without splitting). **`unsafe_code = "forbid"` preserved** by D6's trust-wgpu policy + D1's safe descriptor types — dispatch 119 / 120 / 121 require zero `unsafe` blocks. **Verification gates ALL GREEN**: `cargo +nightly fmt --check` exit 0 (no source touches so trivially clean); Prior: 2026-05-11 (Phase 6 §6.3 Gate C prerequisite dispatch 4 — `RenderInputOwned` + `RenderHandoff` handoff primitive, std-only safe-Rust composition per ADR-117 — substrate landing commit, this): bounded single-agent substrate dispatch extending `crates/editor-shell/src/render_input.rs` (131L → 361L; +230L net) with the latest-only immutable render-input handoff substrate that ADR-117 dispatch-3 pinned the semantics for. **Module placement: extension** to existing `render_input.rs` (NOT a new file — recommended in spec since `RenderInput<'_>` + `RenderInputOwned` + `RenderHandoff` are tightly coupled and `as_render_input()` bridges owned → borrowed). **NEW `RenderInputOwned`** (Clone + Debug): `{ ecs_tick: u64, checkpoint_id: u64, editor_camera: EditorCameraState }` per ADR-117 sub-decision 3 anchor fields + payload. **`RenderInputOwned: Send + 'static`** confirmed automatically (all fields are `Send + 'static`; `EditorCameraState: Copy` is trivially so via glam f32 + Vec3). NO `unsafe`. `as_render_input(&self) -> RenderInput<'_>` borrows back to dispatch-1's view shape. **NEW `RenderHandoff`** (Debug-impl skips lock to stay panic-free under poisoning): `{ slot: std::sync::Mutex<Option<std::sync::Arc<RenderInputOwned>>>, generation: std::sync::atomic::AtomicU64 }` per ADR-117 sub-decision 5 (std-only safe-Rust composition; `arc-swap` escalation deferred until measurement justifies). **`RenderHandoff: Send + Sync`** confirmed automatically. NO `unsafe`. **Public API (additive, all `&self` — no `&mut`)**: `new()` / `Default` (empty slot, generation 0); `publish(snapshot: Arc<RenderInputOwned>)` REPLACES slot then `fetch_add(1, Release)` on generation; `acquire() -> Option<Arc<RenderInputOwned>>` clones the slot Arc; `generation() -> u64` returns `Acquire`-ordered counter for O(1) "did sim publish?" polling without locking the slot. **Latest-only / drop-old**: older Arc strong-counts drop to caller-only once newer publish lands (verified by RH-3 test via `Arc::strong_count`). Render never blocks sim; sim never blocks render beyond the uncontended Mutex briefly held across a single `Arc::clone`. **`crates/editor-shell/src/lib.rs`**: re-export widened from `pub use render_input::RenderInput;` to `pub use render_input::{RenderHandoff, RenderInput, RenderInputOwned};`. **NEW 7 tests** appended to `crates/editor-shell/tests/render_input_boundary.rs` (+178L → 295L total): RIO-1 / RH-1 compile-time `Send + 'static` and `Send + Sync` assertions via inner-fn bounds; RH-2 publish → acquire happy path (`Arc::ptr_eq` confirms same allocation); RH-3 latest-only drop-old (`Arc::strong_count == 1` post-newer-publish); RH-4 generation monotonicity (0 → 1 → 2 → 3); RH-5 empty-slot None; RIO-2 `as_render_input` borrow round-trip with `std::ptr::eq` proving borrow-only. **Constraints honored (LOAD-BEARING)**: NO `unsafe` anywhere; NO new deps (std-only `std::sync::{Mutex, Arc, atomic::AtomicU64}`); NO `wgpu::*` types in either new type; NO `GfxContext` field change; NO `EditorShell` field change; NO `EditorShell` public-API break (additive `pub use` widening only); NO renderer-thread spawn; NO `SnapshotParticipate` impl; NO Gate C empirical mutation test (dispatch 5). **Verification gates ALL GREEN**: `cargo +nightly fmt -p rge-editor-shell` exit 0; `cargo build -p rge-editor-shell` clean; `cargo test -p rge-editor-shell` 11/11 `render_input_boundary` PASS (4 pre-existing + 7 new); `cargo test --workspace --no-fail-fast` = **2371 passed / 0 failed / 19 ignored** (was 2364/0/19; +7 new); `cargo +nightly fmt --check --all` exit 0; `cargo run -q -p rge-tool-architecture-lints -- all` exit 0 (9 enforcement + 1 supplementary PASS, byte-identical). > Snapshot: 2026-05-11 (Phase 6 §6.3 Gate C prerequisite dispatch 3 — render-input handoff mechanism ADR — docs-only design commit, this): **NEW `docs/adr/ADR-117-render-handoff-mechanism.md`** (175L) pins the render-input handoff semantics for the sim/render boundary named by dispatch 1 + regression-protected by dispatch 2. **Decision in one sentence**: latest-only immutable snapshot via `Arc<RenderInputOwned>` with `Send + 'static`; render reads the most-recently-published snapshot at frame-start; sim publishes new snapshots whenever ready; older un-read snapshots are dropped via `Arc` strong-count; render NEVER blocks sim and sim NEVER waits for render. **Five sub-decisions pinned**: (1) handoff semantics = latest-only / drop-old / non-blocking both sides / `(ECS_tick_N, CadCheckpointId_N)` anchor; (2) ownership = `Arc<RenderInputOwned>` with `Send + 'static` bound (future-proofs multi-reader + cross-thread move); (3) anchor = `(ecs_tick, checkpoint_id)` as concrete fields inside `RenderInputOwned` + separate `AtomicU64` generation counter on the handoff substrate; (4) render-lag = latest-only / drop-old (sim publishes K snapshots between two render frames → render sees only the most recent, the older K-1 are dropped); (5) implementation primitive **deliberately deferred to dispatch 4** (the ADR's recommendation: start with std-only safe-Rust composition `Arc<Mutex<Option<Arc<RenderInputOwned>>>>` and escalate to `arc-swap` only if measurement reveals contention — `triple_buffer` 8.1.1 already in `Cargo.lock` as a kira transitive but NOT a workspace-direct dep). **6 alternatives compared in a decision table**: chosen latest-only + manual double-buffer (collapses to chosen once `Arc<_>` ownership applied) + `Arc<RwLock<RenderInputOwned>>` (rejected — violates "render never blocks sim") + channel-with-drop-old (rejected as primary, possible dispatch-4 primitive) + per-frame full clone (rejected — re-introduces synchronous coupling) + `SnapshotParticipate` PIE participant (rejected — PIE is per-tick / cross-process, wrong-shape for per-frame in-process immutability). **`GfxContext` remains render-thread-local-by-`RefCell`** (explicitly preserved; the handoff IS the boundary, the renderer's GPU state stays where it is). **Explicit non-decisions (6)**: wire-format / payload shape (separate ADR); whether dedicated render thread exists today (out of scope); renderer threading model proper (out of scope); `editor_camera`'s final ownership (sim-state vs render-coord-state — deferred to wire-format ADR); whether `gfx.render-snapshot` PIE participant ever materialises (deferred per GFX_RENDER_TIER.md §11.2); specific crate vs std-only primitive (dispatch 4 picks). **Future work captured**: dispatch 4 implementation (NEW `crates/editor-shell/src/render_input/handoff.rs` or analogue, ~150-250 LOC); dispatch 5 §13.6 empirical test (~80-120 LOC); wire-format ADR (sibling); per-field ownership catalogue (in wire-format ADR); PIE participant re-evaluation when wire-format lands. **`docs/architecture/README.md` updated**: ADR count 8 → 9; new line "9 ADRs accepted: ... 116 / 117 (render-handoff mechanism for Gate C)". **HARD NON-GOALS observed (DOCS-ONLY)**: NO `.rs` edits, NO `Cargo.toml` / `Cargo.lock` edits, NO `tools/architecture-lints/**` edits, NO implementation, NO wire-format design, NO architecture-lint changes, NO reopening Gate A/B/PSO-sharing. No `wgpu`, no `gfx`, no `gfx-ir`, no `Device`, no PSO ownership, no texture management — those concerns belong to `rge-gfx` and the (forthcoming) gfx-side adapter (dispatch 2 of 2) that realises a `MaterialDescriptor` into a `gfx::Material` + `PsoKey`. **Five axes**: `ShaderId { Triangle, Mesh, LitMesh }` (matches the three statically-known pipelines in gfx today); `VertexLayoutId { Empty, Vertex, LitVertex }` (Empty = TrianglePipeline, Vertex = MeshPipeline, LitVertex = LitMeshPipeline); `ColorTargetId { Rgba8Unorm, Bgra8UnormSrgb }` (**grounded in real callers** — Grep confirmed those are the only two `wgpu::TextureFormat` values passed to `*::new_cached` in `crates/gfx/src/{pipeline,mesh_pipeline,lit_mesh_pipeline}.rs` today: `Rgba8Unorm` = offscreen `OffscreenTarget`, `Bgra8UnormSrgb` = window swapchain surface; `Rgba8UnormSrgb` appears in `material.rs` for embedded texture storage but is NOT a color attachment); `DepthIntent { None, ReadWrite, ReadOnly }` (today's pipelines all pass `None`; `ReadWrite` and `ReadOnly` are forward-looking for opaque / transparent passes); `MaterialParams { base_color: [f32; 4], phong: [f32; 4] }` (matches the 32-byte UBO shape `gfx::material::Material` uploads: two `vec4<f32>` packed as `(base_color, phong)` where phong = `(ambient, diffuse, specular, shininess)`). All five axes compose into `MaterialDescriptor { shader_id, vertex_layout, color_target, depth, params }`. **All types derive Debug + Clone + Copy + PartialEq + Eq + Hash** (manual Hash on `MaterialParams` via `f32::to_bits()` so the impl is consistent with derived bit-wise PartialEq; +0.0 vs -0.0 are distinct, NaN ≠ NaN — matches PSO-cache identity semantics). `MaterialParams::default()` returns white base colour + zero Phong factors. **Identity contract is LOAD-BEARING**: 6 mandatory unit tests + 2 nice-to-have (`identical_descriptors_are_equal_and_hash_equal` / per-axis distinctness on each of the 5 axes / `material_descriptor_clone_preserves_identity` / `default_material_params_is_white_no_phong`); all 8 pass. **HARD NON-GOALS observed**: ZERO `wgpu` / `gfx` / `gfx-ir` dependency added (verified `git diff -- crates/material-runtime/Cargo.toml` byte-identical); ZERO new public exports from any other crate; ZERO edits to gfx / gfx-ir / brep-render / cad-projection / cad-core / editor-shell / rge-editor; no PSO key construction; no shader hash; no vertex layout descriptor; no TextureId / TextureBindingIntent; no `serde` derives (no consumer; workspace doctrine doesn't force them on intent types); no new ADRs / new lints / new exemptions. **`//! With sub-α + sub-β + sub-γ all in place, the chapter has the **complete headless** chain: `world.query::<BRepHandle>()` → `render_mesh_for(entity)` produces RenderMesh per entity, AND `screen_to_world_ray + pick_face` produces FaceSelection — all referring to the SAME face-identity space (the chain-consistency test verifies this). Prior: editor-shell sub-β shipped: NEW `crates/editor-shell/src/camera.rs` module with `pub struct CameraView { view_proj: glam::Mat4, viewport_size: [f32; 2] }` + `CameraView::screen_to_world_ray(screen_pos: [f32; 2]) -> Option<rge_cad_projection::picking::Ray>` — a CPU-only screen→world unproject primitive that turns (screen pixel + caller-composed view*projection matrix + viewport size) into the existing picker's `Ray` shape. Independent of `rge_gfx::Camera` (which is GPU-only and not CPU-readable). **NDC convention LOAD-BEARING**: `view_proj` assumed wgpu/Vulkan/D3D (Z ∈ 0..1), matching `glam::Mat4::perspective_rh()` (NOT `_gl` variants which use Z ∈ -1..+1). **Y-flip**: `screen_pos` in winit top-left convention; NDC Y flipped on the way in (`ndc_y = 1.0 - 2.0 * (screen_y / viewport_h)`). **Algorithm**: screen → NDC, inverse view_proj with finiteness check (returns None on non-invertible / NaN-inf), unproject NDC near (Z=0) and far (Z=1) clip points, perspective-divide on `w` (returns None if either w is zero), build Ray with `direction = far - near` (NOT normalised — matches the picker's contract). **Layering — editor-shell is editor-tier (NOT renderer-tier)**: `forbidden-dep` rule 6 (RENDERER_CRATES → game-domain forbidden) does NOT apply, so editor-shell gains `rge-cad-projection` as a PRODUCTION dep (Tier-2 editor → Tier-2 game-domain via the picker module's Ray re-export). `glam = "0.30"` added as production dep matching gfx's existing version (no bytemuck feature — editor-shell never touches GPU buffers). **7 unit tests** in `camera.rs::tests` (identity_view_proj_screen_center_yields_ray_through_origin / identity_view_proj_top_left_corner_ray_origin_at_top_left_ndc / viewport_y_flip_correctness / perspective_camera_origin_at_5_screen_center_ray_through_origin / direction_is_not_normalized_per_picker_ray_contract / degenerate_zero_view_proj_returns_none / near_plane_z_is_zero_per_wgpu_convention) + **3 integration tests** in NEW `crates/editor-shell/tests/camera_picker_smoke.rs` (camera_view_screen_center_picks_cuboid_top_face / camera_view_off_axis_screen_pos_misses_centered_cuboid / camera_view_composes_into_face_selection_set — the third demonstrates the full `CameraView → Ray → pick_face → FaceSelection → EditorCoord.face_selection` chain). The integration tests construct `CadGraph` / `CadProjection` / `World` / `BRepHandle` with the same pattern as `crates/cad-projection/tests/face_picking_smoke.rs`. The second piece of the Render-backed face-selection chapter (active 2026-05-10) — turns "screen pixel + camera state → world ray" from a pen-and-paper formula into a callable, tested, headless primitive. **Does NOT bring up rendering**: no GPU, no winit event handler, no surface, no `gfx::Camera` modification, no `EditorShell::window_event` modification (mouse-event wiring is sub-δ).
